  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a3eff6db-a9f5-4243-ad27-fcb842269a89'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<div id="review_860396160" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/860396160" />
    <a title="Dearbhla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3611893-dearbhla"><img alt="Dearbhla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1273273738p2/3611893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/860396160?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dearbhla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dearbhla" href="/user/show/3611893-dearbhla">Dearbhla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3611893-dearbhla?shelf=sff">sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3611893-dearbhla?shelf=juv-ya">juv-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer860396160" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8929890377697764840">I am miles and miles and miles away from being obsessive and compulsive, yet I do have a completion-ist streak in me. That is the only excuse I offer for continuing to read this series of books. It isn’t that they are bad, or horrible. There is nothing Meyer-Twilight-horrific enough to keep me reading because I just can’t look away from the wrongness of it all. But at the same time, this is not a good book.<br/>Action and adventure and flying horses. That’s why I read the first one. Why I read the se</span>
  <span id="freeText8929890377697764840" style="display:none">I am miles and miles and miles away from being obsessive and compulsive, yet I do have a completion-ist streak in me. That is the only excuse I offer for continuing to read this series of books. It isn’t that they are bad, or horrible. There is nothing Meyer-Twilight-horrific enough to keep me reading because I just can’t look away from the wrongness of it all. But at the same time, this is not a good book.<br />Action and adventure and flying horses. That’s why I read the first one. Why I read the second… well, it could have improved. It didn’t really, but it was more of the same. Enough to let me know that while this series of books was perfectly adequate for certain tastes, it wasn’t for mine. I like character. Well drawn characters. This does not have that.<br />It has a very simplistic plot and very simplistic characters. I don’t write that to knock the book. That is what it is aiming to be, I think and hope :) and there is nothing wrong with children’s books being just that. Of course the very best of children’s books have layers and complexity. This doesn’t.<br />It is a simple story, and it is told in an entertaining fashion. With battles and action galore. It has people standing up for what they believe in, occasionally they may not do the “correct” thing, but they try to do the right thing. So it’ll pass an afternoon, and I think that if I was a child this would be a book that I would love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8929890377697764840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1038412227" />
    <a title="Nancy Morales" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34220500-nancy-morales"><img alt="Nancy Morales" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431389165p2/34220500.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1038412227?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1038412227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16151318750604375205">This book is as great as the series. It has romance, action, and mostly greek mythology mythology mixed in with the modern world.I love this book because it shows that anyone can be a hero and fight for what they think is right. It made me feel suspense each time I wanted to stop, but I couldn't! It really made me keep the page turning and not wanting me to stop reading till the book ended. I mostly enjoyed when the CRU, a secret agency made clones of the Gods and goddesses of Olympus, its cruel</span>
  <span id="freeText16151318750604375205" style="display:none">This book is as great as the series. It has romance, action, and mostly greek mythology mythology mixed in with the modern world.I love this book because it shows that anyone can be a hero and fight for what they think is right. It made me feel suspense each time I wanted to stop, but I couldn't! It really made me keep the page turning and not wanting me to stop reading till the book ended. I mostly enjoyed when the CRU, a secret agency made clones of the Gods and goddesses of Olympus, its cruel of me to like that but it made me enjoy when the real gods meet the clones. Once it gets to that part, it makes you not want to stop until it has ended or even till one remained victorious. Kate describes each character with a detail that makes you imagine the character as if you could see them right in front of you. When I read how she descried described Cupid, I thought of him as a really cute guy, maybe even better any guy that I've ever seen, not to offend anyone though. I would say go right ahead and read this adventurous book that filled with romance, adventure, and suspense, however that's up to you to choose to read it or leave it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16151318750604375205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3229331473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3229331473" />
    <a title="Clare O&#39;Beara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23233462-clare-o-beara"><img alt="Clare O&#39;Beara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585485276p2/23233462.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3229331473?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clare O&#39;Beara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clare O&#39;Beara" href="/user/show/23233462-clare-o-beara">Clare O&#39;Beara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23233462-clare-o-beara?shelf=fantasy-urban">fantasy-urban</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23233462-clare-o-beara?shelf=america-fiction">america-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23233462-clare-o-beara?shelf=horse-fiction">horse-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23233462-clare-o-beara?shelf=young-adult-sff">young-adult-sff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3229331473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10125859604684412387">I had not read the earlier books and quite a lot needs explaining to me still, after finishing this read. Where exactly is Olympus, how did Emily get there and how did she becomes beloved of the winged horse? The Olympians, the characters from Greek myth, need to partake of ambrosia - who makes this? Emily goes back to Earth because in a story line out of The Black Stallion, a wonder horse is burning up the tracks and it looks like Emily's winged horse. <br/><br/>Then the small team she brings, discover t</span>
  <span id="freeText10125859604684412387" style="display:none">I had not read the earlier books and quite a lot needs explaining to me still, after finishing this read. Where exactly is Olympus, how did Emily get there and how did she becomes beloved of the winged horse? The Olympians, the characters from Greek myth, need to partake of ambrosia - who makes this? Emily goes back to Earth because in a story line out of The Black Stallion, a wonder horse is burning up the tracks and it looks like Emily's winged horse. <br /><br />Then the small team she brings, discover that there are clones of some of the mythological beasts and beings, which they all decry as unnatural. Excuse me, you're riding a flying horse whose brother is a flying boar and you're accompanied by a Sphinx. We're in 'Companions of Xanth' territory. <br /><br />An author simultaneously has an easy job using Greek myth - the characters and relationships are already written - and a tough one, because how to reconcile all the craziness, the powers of gods, the interaction with humans - and how to make it original? <br /><br />I just wanted to read about a winged horse, instead of that I got a book about superheroes (which I almost never read) and a massive body count, and fast and loose cloning. How come nobody cloned a female winged horse? That would be easy to do by leaving out a Y chromosome. We actually get almost nothing about the science of genetics. Still, young readers may be interested in finding out more about the facts. The adventure is dramatic and pretty violent. <br />This is an unbiased review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10125859604684412387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11852817611524427753">Pegasus and the New Olympians by Kate O Hearn is an exciting novel full of mystery and excitement. It was much more intriguing than the first two books in the series and i never wanted to put it down. It begins in olympus, where Emily and her friends must go down to earth due to the CRU cloning the olympians. It started out with another pegasus, and slowly grew until there were multiple Paleans, Joels, and more. Emily and her crew must try to stop them before these dangerous olympians destroy Ne</span>
  <span id="freeText11852817611524427753" style="display:none">Pegasus and the New Olympians by Kate O Hearn is an exciting novel full of mystery and excitement. It was much more intriguing than the first two books in the series and i never wanted to put it down. It begins in olympus, where Emily and her friends must go down to earth due to the CRU cloning the olympians. It started out with another pegasus, and slowly grew until there were multiple Paleans, Joels, and more. Emily and her crew must try to stop them before these dangerous olympians destroy New York. When the team is split up they must figure out what to do in pairs. I would recommend this book to people who enjoy very suspenseful fantasy novel. I would rate this book 5\5. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1875487383" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melinda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melinda" href="/user/show/611813-melinda">Melinda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/611813-melinda?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/611813-melinda?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/611813-melinda?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/611813-melinda?shelf=juvenile-lit">juvenile-lit</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1875487383&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1875487383" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3762046512305822638">One of my young friends recommended this book, actually the entire series, because I love horses and she does too. She also enjoys riddles, which I enjoy too, and there are several in this book provided by the wonderful character of the Sphinx! I found it to be a hat-tip to the Percy Jackson books (written by Rick Riordan) in a very positive way, while focusing on Pegasus and his special relationship with his human friend, Emily.<br/><br/>I was surprised that this had a bit more grim and dark themes -- Ar</span>
  <span id="freeText3762046512305822638" style="display:none">One of my young friends recommended this book, actually the entire series, because I love horses and she does too. She also enjoys riddles, which I enjoy too, and there are several in this book provided by the wonderful character of the Sphinx! I found it to be a hat-tip to the Percy Jackson books (written by Rick Riordan) in a very positive way, while focusing on Pegasus and his special relationship with his human friend, Emily.<br /><br />I was surprised that this had a bit more grim and dark themes -- Area 51, cloning aliens (and the subsequent "failed clones" that happen before you get a "successful clone"), torture, and horrific mutilation of clones. It reminded me a bit of the rather dismal movie, "Alien Resurrection" where Ridley is confronted with her own clones, living but terribly deformed, who beg to be destroyed. Not exactly the association I would have thought would be there.<br /><br />So while I enjoyed Pegasus and his relationship with Emily, and I enjoyed the combination of Olympic gods into our world.... this was not a book I would want to read again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3762046512305822638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16389016535959741963" style="display:none"> In Emily’s last adventure she went back to earth and saved her father Steve.   <span id="freeText10602692215766040949" style="display:none"><b>Synopsis:</b> <i>"When reports reach Olympus of a Pegasus 'double' sighted on Earth, suspicions are aroused. Emily and Pegasus must fly back to her world where they discover a sinister conspiracy that will pit Olympian against human in a war involving friends and enemies on either side."</i><br /><br /><b>My Review:</b> I rather enjoyed this series when it first started out but it has progressively gone down hill for me. Not to mention we have gone from a myth and urban fantasy storyline to a more sci-fi based elements. The book really dragged for me and I had to force myself to continue reading it and finish the book. It was rather slow moving with too many things pulling apart and then of course all is miraculously resolved but don't worry more of the same danger is coming for the next book in the series (which I will not be reading).</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1297948352455115009">Fantastically written...the characters just leapt off the page. I enjoyed every moment of this. Despite it's classification as middle-grade/young adult there is just something about this book that I think will appeal to all ages.<br/><br/>I am a huge fan of books about mythology and simply can't get enough of them. What a fantastic find. Eagerly awaiting reading the next instalment.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2746318461" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24522818-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590570778p2/24522818.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2746318461?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/24522818-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781442444157" href="/book/show/20028153-the-new-olympians">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2746318461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14721408726586843290">Marked spoiler at the end, but otherwise a safe review. I give this 3.5 stars, rounding down to 3. While I thoroughly enjoyed the first two books, this one just doesn’t do it for me. It’s been three books of the same enemy and while I still like Emily for the most part, her willful ignorance is beginning to grate on me.<br/><br/>She’s been thrown headfirst into the world of mythology, sure, but she’s practically worshipped by the Olympians. She recognizes her importance yet does she pick up a book to lear</span>
  <span id="freeText14721408726586843290" style="display:none">Marked spoiler at the end, but otherwise a safe review. I give this 3.5 stars, rounding down to 3. While I thoroughly enjoyed the first two books, this one just doesn’t do it for me. It’s been three books of the same enemy and while I still like Emily for the most part, her willful ignorance is beginning to grate on me.<br /><br />She’s been thrown headfirst into the world of mythology, sure, but she’s practically worshipped by the Olympians. She recognizes her importance yet does she pick up a book to learn about her new people? Noooo. I get that the author is using her ignorance as a tool to explain mythology, but there are ways to do it without making her ignorant to the point of frustration. <br /><br />Everything else in this book...... was just okay. It was oddly paced, there was random jealousy, and the decisions characters made didn’t make much sense to me. The whole book was just chaos and felt poorly planned out. It was also quite dark in a way that was altogether unexpected and unnecessary in a children’s book, especially when that darkness was mostly glanced over.<br /><br />It’s hard for me to pinpoint what exactly ruined this book for me, but in general it didn’t quite sit well. I plan on finishing the series still, but I’m unsure if I’d still recommend it. There were just too many wtf moments as I was reading it.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />*****Tiny Spoiler Here*****<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />In my review of the last book I mentioned how excited I was that Kate O’Hearn had kept Emily’s leg injury because it was a great to see a heroine with a physical disadvantage still kick ass. But in this book she just magically decides her leg is okay and magically it is and I’m so mad about it. Kate lost a lot of points with me over this. <br /><br />Well, that and how Joel’s arm (after he basically had it amputated) was replaced by a fully functional even better one. The author had the chance to provide representation and she didn’t even try.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14721408726586843290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Michelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/103105075-michelle"><img alt="Michelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569164333p2/103105075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2986362381?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle" href="/user/show/103105075-michelle">Michelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2986362381&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2986362381" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2666094878922502579">I found the first two books rather enjoyable to read, but I think it was around this book that the series started to be... just okay. There's just so many convenient elements of the story that were put in just to eliminate the problems in the first few books, and Emily is legitimately now TOO overpowered. The fact that literally everything in the series HAS to be about Emily makes it almost frustrating. The Olympians basically worship Emily, give her everything she ever wanted and every single n</span>
  <span id="freeText2666094878922502579" style="display:none">I found the first two books rather enjoyable to read, but I think it was around this book that the series started to be... just okay. There's just so many convenient elements of the story that were put in just to eliminate the problems in the first few books, and Emily is legitimately now TOO overpowered. The fact that literally everything in the series HAS to be about Emily makes it almost frustrating. The Olympians basically worship Emily, give her everything she ever wanted and every single new thing is a result of her in some way. Everything is centered around her and while that is not necessarily a bad thing, this series just does not do a good job of it.<br /><br />Like how does Emily just "will" her leg to be okay?? And all these random new powers just seem to be there for the convenience of it being there which is extremely frustrating and unnecessarily makes Emily some overpowered entity. Also, how does she not bother to understand a single thing about the Olympians? I know this is for the readers that do not know mythology and all that but we don't need to make Emily more hate-able than she already is.<br /><br />This review seems really harsh but it's just disappointing to see promising series turn so... just okay.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2666094878922502579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1361545682742590117">Pegasus and the New Olympians is the 3rd book in the Pegasus series. Emily and Pegasus have another journey and this time they have to go back to earth. As Emily and Pegasus get word that there have been Olympian look alike on earth. They are determined to figure out why and how! As they come back to earth they have to be so careful so they don't get caught by CRU. They get help from other Olympians.   <span id="freeText1361545682742590117" style="display:none">Pegasus and the New Olympians is the 3rd book in the Pegasus series. Emily and Pegasus have another journey and this time they have to go back to earth. As Emily and Pegasus get word that there have been Olympian look alike on earth. They are determined to figure out why and how! As they come back to earth they have to be so careful so they don't get caught by CRU. They get help from other Olympians. They found out that the CRU when they captured them last time they were on earth took there blood and cloned them. Zesus finds and out and their is a huge war. They take the clones back to Olympus and treat them as family.<br /><br />The theme in this book is that never give up. They had to try so hard to figure out what was going on and they almost got killed and caught multiple times! I would recommend this book to everyone. I loved it! Such a good book and has everything in one.... Love, comedy, drama and more! If you haven't read it, do it!!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17715863107673422295">This was definitely an improvement over the second book. I'm still on the fence whether it exceeds the original or not.<br/><br/>One thing I have noticed is that with good storytellers, they often find a way for the protagonist to dig themselves deeper into problems before a resolution presents themselves. This book definitely had this...at various points, I wanted to beg Emily not to make the decisions she did. Often the mark of a engrossing plot.<br/><br/>I will say that Kate O'Hearn addressed one of my big compl</span>
  <span id="freeText17715863107673422295" style="display:none">This was definitely an improvement over the second book. I'm still on the fence whether it exceeds the original or not.<br /><br />One thing I have noticed is that with good storytellers, they often find a way for the protagonist to dig themselves deeper into problems before a resolution presents themselves. This book definitely had this...at various points, I wanted to beg Emily not to make the decisions she did. Often the mark of a engrossing plot.<br /><br />I will say that Kate O'Hearn addressed one of my big complaints from the last book, which was the fact that Emily's leg was healed when she became the Flame in the first book. Yet, there she was in the second book with a gimpy leg again. This is explained to some extent here in the third book.<br /><br />And we have been left with some unknown plot points, no doubt to entice you to continue on with the series.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText1439506159862532756" style="display:none">I’m over 70 pages in, and I give up. I read some of the reviews, and it sounds like it’s not going to get any better. <br /><br />I loved how Emily’s leg was not healed at the end of the first book. In the second book, she had some trouble, but not as much as I expected. Now she can walk just as well as she used to be able too. Even worse, Joel’s new arm has super strength. <br /><br />The plot of this book is just ridiculous, and some of the characters make decisions that don’t make much sense. I’m a bit confused as to how Emily doesn’t know more about her new world yet, or why she’s not better able to communicate with Pegasus by now. Then there was the new character of Alexis, who acted annoying and seemed really spoiled. <br /><br />The only thing I liked was that the aunt, who I thought had been forgotten about, was acknowledged.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1980717964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8912088309871049059">This is a very good YA series. Lots of good life lessons, while coming to grips with the fact that you now have amazing super powers that can be used for good or bad It is empowering and sad, at the same time, as our hero Emily, realizes that she can kill the bad guys if she wants to. That's a heavy burden to place on anyone, let alone a teenager. I thoght that the author did a very credible job with this dilemna.<br/><br/>Loads of action in this one. A good read.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7144339867202671247">my favorite character is Alexis because she is so brave and loyal to Emily. what suprised me most was that Jupiter found out that Emily went to olympus but then decided not to turn the solar stream on Earth. I would not change the ending because I love it when pegasus comes back and then Jupiter did not turn on Earth.</span>

  <span id="freeText10344432460181356337" style="display:none">In the book Pegasus: The New Olympians by Kate O'hearn, The main character Emily discovers that the "CREW" Were making clones of the Olympians. The only one she knew of was the clone of her beloved Pegasus. The clone was known to be the fastest "horse" in the world. She knew she had to stop them from making any more. People have heard of Olympians causing chaos around Las Vegas. She goes and stops them from making even more Olympians to cause more worry throughout the town. When she is there, she realized that they were trying to make a Olympian of her. I would recommend this book to grades 5-8. It is a great book and you will just have to read it to be able to know what happens to Emily. Will she be one of a kind? Or have a instinct to kill her clone? Find out in the book Pegasus: The New Olympians.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h3DDWwORVeaMWCHoLY1hiCxFET3mNtEdcEx/Y5ARRsJ5KWuBOAzq2S647Mq1vqQaKARlynXqbZAjzKojuLQQjQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vubWg3ZuqIunsu1X+KIKqVYEHOReROkSpWqWch0ABgJAv35ZTfMXtAVSIHVgkc87UkVoE82YVZ/26kMyNaVQTQ==')})
  }

The Guardian Herd: Starfire tells the thrilling story of<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16621856641027511088\" style=\"display:none\">Fans of the Warriors, Survivors, and Guardians of Ga’Hoole series will love this first book in an action-packed tween fantasy series about winged horses from debut author Jennifer Lynn Alvarez. The Guardian Herd: Starfire tells the thrilling story of a young foal, Star, who controls the fate of the land of Anok and the five pegasi herds that live there.\n\nOnce every hundred years, a black foal is born, prophesized to either unite or destroy the five herds of flying horses that live in the land of Anok. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11565272993688198694">Kate O'Hearn was born in Toronto Canada, but raised in the heart of New York City and has lived in many places throughout her life. These days, she calls the south coast of England home. She has 3 brothers, no sisters and is passionate about animals and their causes and has many animal friends. (Pets)<br/><br/>Over the course of her life she has had several careers before finding her real love, writing chil</span>
  <span id="freeText11565272993688198694" style="display:none">Kate O'Hearn was born in Toronto Canada, but raised in the heart of New York City and has lived in many places throughout her life. These days, she calls the south coast of England home. She has 3 brothers, no sisters and is passionate about animals and their causes and has many animal friends. (Pets)<br /><br />Over the course of her life she has had several careers before finding her real love, writing children's books. Being the only girl in family of boys, she grew up a true tom-boy and always loved books with high adventure. But one of the problems she discovered was a lack of female leads in these adventure books.<br /><br />When she started to write, Kate decided to address this imbalance and now writes high fantasy adventures with strong, compassionate and adventure loving girl heroes. There are plenty of boys in the story to keep it interesting and challenging, but she believes that a girl hero can be as brave, strong and adventurous as a boy.<br /><br />She insists that adventures are for everyone!<br /><br />So come and enjoy a few adventures with her...</span>
  <a data-text-id="11565272993688198694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
